<username>Tony Park< /username><review>Read for a thorough and honest review of SoCal Barber, a brand new barber shop serving the local Norwalk and Downey Community!

SoCal Barber needs to be your go-to barbershop in the Norwalk-Downey Community.  The owners opened their brand-new shop with a mission and passion to give the highest quality cuts to their customers.  I can attest that this shop will not disappoint, the customer service sets the highest standard of what competing barber shops should offer.  With more than seven seats and a talented barber to fill each one, you will never have to wait long and will leave looking your absolute freshest. With more than thirty combined years of barbershop experience, the owners strive to give the BEST cuts to their customers.

The shop is modern and welcoming; you immediately walk in to a row of brand new seats, husky toolboxes, and big screen TVs.  The magic is in the details as each barber apron adorns the SoCal logo.

SoCal Barber easily rates a 5 out of 5 for customer service, the owner has a motto that everyone should be treated as family; each customer is offered a bottle of water.

SoCal treats military and first responders very well

Bottom line or TLDR:  This is the best new barbershop in town.  I receive a high quality cut every single week, the price is competitive, the barbers are talented, and the customer service is on point.  Look no further, this is the one.

< text>
Appalling and horrendous.  That's the only way to describe my experience.  Yesterday, as I was riding my bike past Dr. Domotor's around 4:45pm, I noticed that there was a dead parrot in the grass in front of the "Animal Hospital".  I figured some low-life that couldn't be bothered to properly dispose of it had left it there to make it another person's problem.  Well, it became mine.

I went inside and told the lady at the front desk that there was a dead parrot outside of the building.  When she looked at me like she didn't know what to do, I offered to bring it inside if she gave me a box and a pair of gloves.  A lady came out in scrubs, and the first lady asked her if she would take care of it.  Her response was "I'm off the clock.  Can't you call Animal Control?"  The first lady then thanked me for telling them and assured me they would take care of it.

Well, I guess everyone was off the clock.  They didn't do anything, not even call Animal Control.  In this case, that would be the Pasadena Humane Society and SPCA.  I called them this morning after I walked past the building and the bird was still there.  When I called Dr. Domotor's to let them know what happened, I didn't even get a response, they just hung up on me without saying anything.

To make it clear, I would have been willing to take care of the bird myself in other circumstances.  Years ago, driving past a restaurant I worked at (on my day off), I noticed a dead cat in the road in front of the building.  I stopped, borrowed a shovel, and buried the cat away from the building.  Had I not, there's no telling how long it would have been there.  It's also less likely that the litter of kittens with her, which were still alive, would have been saved.  I don't usually carry a shovel on my bike, and I wasn't about to put a dead parrot in my pocket so I could rub it with my thumb like Lenny Small.

I also understand that you might be wary about a dead animal, and want to take certain precautions before exposing it to other animals.  There is absolutely no excuse for just leaving a dead animal in front of an "Animal Hospital" overnight, or even for ten minutes.  Perhaps at least somebody there has a brain and genuine concern for animals, but at least three don't.  If you take your pets there, good luck with the ones that end up handling them.</text>

<Name>Brooks Keys</Name><time>1326839930107< /time>< Rating>

< review>
Domotor's Doggie Dachau

I left my 10 1/2 year old spayed Lab for three nights kenneling.  I took two standard bed pillows in sewn-together cases, a cotton throw rug that goes on top of the pillows, and in a large zip-lock a T-shirt I'd worn to provide my scent, a squeaky toy, and several large crunchy bones. I verbally asked them to place the pillow in her kennel and to give the dog the T-shirt, squeaky toy, and one crunchy bone per day.  The assistant acknowledged this.  The vet's assistant removed my dog's collar and scarf and gave them to me, saying they could be a choke hazard.  (It's the first time I'd had this occur for kenneling - there must have been a tragic experience in the past, but better safe than sorry)  I inspected the individual kennel my dog was in.  It was very clean and had a clean blanket on the concrete floor.  I was not allowed to open the gate and place the pillows inside, but was assured my dog would have them.

After the three nights I returned for my dog.  The dog was as healthy as when I left her.  I put her collar back on and asked for the pillows, T-shirt, etc. In a jiffy the assistant returned with the pillows, rug, and zip-lock.  The zip-lock contained the T-shirt, squeaky toy, and ALL of the crunchy bones.  The T-shirt, pillows, and rug had no dog hair on them.

I highly suspect that my pure bred, ACK-papers, house-dog had to sleep on a blanket over concrete with nothing to remind her of 10 1/2 years with her owner, or hope that she would be reunited with me.  My dog is healthy and Dr. Domnotor's kennel is very clean.  I have no complaint about the safety or sanitation of the kennels.  But I think I sent my dog to a Doggy Dachau. My mom has been going to Dr Demotor for 15 years. We moved during that time and have tried new vets that are closer. Every time we try a new vet we end up taking the animal back to Dr. Demotor because the other vets don't have the experience or knowledge about taking care of tricky issues. We have a dog with a gum infection we took her to another vet for 3 years and she lost over half her teeth. We got fed up and took her to Dr Domotor and the infection was clear within a few months. I have a cat who got into a fight. I tried taking her to VCA and they didnt find the puncture wounds. Because they didnt find the wounds the first time bacteria festered under her skin and now, a week later, she is loosing almost half of the skin on her back. The doctors at Dr Domotors office decided to take a skin culture to be sure that we were fighting the disease with the right antibiotics. No to mention they remembered to give me painkillers... Yea Dr. Domotor is expensive but it's a sure way to guarantee that your pet will get proper treatment by experienced professionals. You wont spend all your money visiting the vet for the same reason over and over. I hope they stay in business for as long as my cat will live.<//review>

< review>
This is a quaint little Izakaya tucked in the corner of a larger shopping center. I am told they are one of the best lunch places in the area. I went for dinner. Food was as expected, and the atmosphere was nice. The "normal" stuff really shined as the best, soba noodles, fresh tofu, sliced meat.
I give it 4 stars rather than 5 because they are a little understaffed for dinner. We had a reservation for 6:30pm, and when we arrived they told us we had to be out by 8pm (very short for a $50+ per person meal). They also mixed up one of our orders (ordered white tuna, served yellow tail).<//review>

Makenzie Delarosa< /user_name>
< Review>
The first time I've known about Leichi was when my boyfriend and I were in the area and had to find the nearest supermarket. We found the Lucky's off San Tomas Expressway, and then I saw Leichi located in the corner of the plaza. I mistook Leichi for a boba cafe, but I discovered that it was actually a sit-down Japanese restaurant. When I got home I did a bit of research on the restaurant and was impressed by the menu, which looked phenomenal. I had to give the place a try next time.

I thought Leichi was going to be a fancy restaurant based on the gourmet quality of the menu items that I saw online. Contrary to my belief it was way more casual than I expected, and the restaurant was small too.

I made a lunch reservation for myself via Yelp on a Monday at 11:30am. Good thing I made a reservation! I was surprised by how busy it was especially when the place literally just opened. All the tables that could accommodate parties of 3+ were occupied. Staff members were even advising walk-in customers to make reservations, because they were booked for lunch. I had no issues with checking in though. There was an available seat for me right at the sushi bar.

The customer service was pretty standard for what I expect from an Asian restaurant. The servers were friendly. My waitress wasn't very attentive after she asked for my drink and entree order, but it wasn't a make or break for me.

I ordered the Leichi Premium Lunch Special. For $24 I got a side of rice along with 7 different Japanese tapas including miso soup, sashimi, steam egg custard, baked salmon, an assortment of pickled vegetables, silken tofu, and a mixed grill. Yes, the Premium Lunch special was expensive but absolutely worth the splurge! The tapas came out in a simple but beautifully thoughtful presentation, but most importantly the Premium Lunch Special was overall delicious.

Leichi's miso soup was a great starter. It had some seaweed pieces and small pieces of soft tofu in the broth.

The pickled veggies were nice to eat in between the tapas to reset my palette. The veggies included carrots, cucumbers, daikon, and brussel sprouts.

All 4 pieces of my sashimi were hamachi (yellow tail). The fish tasted very fresh, and the pieces were thick.

The baked salmon was excellent. I think it was marinaded in some type of teriyaki or miso sauce. The salmon was light, flaky, and moist.

There was a tapas with a mix of grilled beef flank, onions, and pieces of parsnip or turnip. They were all in a ponzu type of sauce, and it was served cold.

One of the tapas came in a cup, which I thought was going to be the steamed egg custard. I was surprised to find that it was a cup of house-made silken tofu with pork pieces instead. The tofu was delicate and slightly savory, but the pork pieces were what packed the saltiness.

The steam egg custard was so unique. The way the egg was prepared reminded me of egg drop soup, but the egg pulls were long and stringy. It came in a sweet and savory broth, and there were bits of bamboo shoots.</Review>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
The first time I've known about Leichi was when my boyfriend and I were in the area and had to find the nearest supermarket. We found the Lucky's off San Tomas Expressway, and then I saw Leichi located in the corner of the plaza. I mistook Leichi for a boba cafe, but I discovered that it was actually a sit-down Japanese restaurant. When I got home I did a bit of research on the restaurant and was impressed by the menu, which looked phenomenal. I had to give the place a try next time.

I thought Leichi was going to be a fancy restaurant based on the gourmet quality of the menu items that I saw online. Contrary to my belief it was way more casual than I expected, and the restaurant was small too.

I made a lunch reservation for myself via Yelp on a Monday at 11:30am. Good thing I made a reservation! I was surprised by how busy it was especially when the place literally just opened. All the tables that could accommodate parties of 3+ were occupied. Staff members were even advising walk-in customers to make reservations, because they were booked for lunch. I had no issues with checking in though. There was an available seat for me right at the sushi bar.

The customer service was pretty standard for what I expect from an Asian restaurant. The servers were friendly. My waitress wasn't very attentive after she asked for my drink and entree order, but it wasn't a make or break for me.

I ordered the Leichi Premium Lunch Special. For $24 I got a side of rice along with 7 different Japanese tapas including miso soup, sashimi, steam egg custard, baked salmon, an assortment of pickled vegetables, silken tofu, and a mixed grill. Yes, the Premium Lunch special was expensive but absolutely worth the splurge! The tapas came out in a simple but beautifully thoughtful presentation, but most importantly the Premium Lunch Special was overall delicious.

Leichi's miso soup was a great starter. It had some seaweed pieces and small pieces of soft tofu in the broth.

The pickled veggies were nice to eat in between the tapas to reset my palette. The veggies included carrots, cucumbers, daikon, and brussel sprouts.

All 4 pieces of my sashimi were hamachi (yellow tail). The fish tasted very fresh, and the pieces were thick.

The baked salmon was excellent. I think it was marinaded in some type of teriyaki or miso sauce. The salmon was light, flaky, and moist.

There was a tapas with a mix of grilled beef flank, onions, and pieces of parsnip or turnip. They were all in a ponzu type of sauce, and it was served cold.

One of the tapas came in a cup, which I thought was going to be the steamed egg custard. I was surprised to find that it was a cup of house-made silken tofu with pork pieces instead. The tofu was delicate and slightly savory, but the pork pieces were what packed the saltiness.

The steam egg custard was so unique. The way the egg was prepared reminded me of egg drop soup, but the egg pulls were long and stringy. It came in a sweet and savory broth, and there were bits of bamboo shoots.<//review>

<Text>I love this place.

My girlfriend decided to give this little Izakaya joint a try after our trip to Santana Row and boy were we surprised. We were excited to eat here because we love Japanese food but this place blew our expectations out of the water. We ordered about 6-8 different dishes and our favorite was the Chazuke. Although the dish is simple in nature, it was just so good here. Definitely will get this when we come back. There were some other great dishes, such as their Sesame Tofu that's made in house and their Plum Juice.

The staff was great as well. I got the sense that they were a bit inexperienced and are looking to improve, but I couldn't help but feel their sincerity through our interactions. This was no Michelin starred experience, but they definitely added to the dining experience.

I'm going to be back here every time I find myself in the SJ area.<//Text><gmapID>0x808fcaf39c1c7265:0x607b1c94f168d3b5<//gmapID>< Time>

<username>Sherry Li</username><Resp>None< /Resp>< pictures>
None<//pictures>
< text>
I've been eyeing Leichi on Yelp ever since I moved down to the South Bay. I finally made the trip a few weeks ago and was not disappointed.

You can make a reservation on Yelp, which is great. The restaurant is quite small, maybe only 15-20 seats, so don't be a dummy and make a resy (TM pending)!

Because we went at opening, we were able to get the freshly made tofu and one of the 10 available batches of freshly made soba. We also got the takowasa, the broiled gindara, mushroom tempura, and the strawberry panna cotta for dessert.

Is it too cliche to say everything was perfect and delicious?

The tofu came with the traditional toppings - soy sauce, ginger, salt, scallions, and shredded katsubushi. The soba we got with the kamo nanban broth, which was subtle yet flavorful. The mushroom tempura came with a green tea salt, and it was really interesting (in a good way)! And you can't go wrong with broiled gindara. It was not under or overcooked and the sweet miso marinade complemented the subtle sweetness of the fish really well.

Definitely want to come back for the omakase!<//text>

< review>
Update: Had their take-out food recently. Very tasty and carefully packaged. Good portions. The bento box consisted of the main protein, small green salad, potato salad, pickles, rice, and cooked vegetables. Fantastic value.

Authentic izakaya (small gastropub)! This is not a sushi house. Order both the cooked items and sashimi. The menu is extensive and pay attention to the handwritten menu items posted on the wall. Lunch is cash-only, but dinner is credit card-ok.

***Note that this restaurant opened in 2015. The location was formerly occupied by Hoshi, also a Japanese izakaya. Google+ hasn't eliminated the reviews for Hoshi and mixed them up with Leichi's. Hoshi had some issues with their dinner servers. However, at Leichi, service is very attentive.***<//review>

WWWWAAAAAAYYYYY in the corner, tucked back and basically forgotten in terms of the draw to the center. You literally can't see the sign when going West along the outer shop until it's all up on you.

Prices are stable and standard for most peet's. They do a salted carmel machiatto thingy and so trying to replicate the sea salt iced coffee from 85 Degree's I ahad them salt the latte on my green tea. Horibble failure. Granted I tried to sweeten it myself it tasted like seaweed and not the good savory roasted kind or even Costco brand. Like a milky iodine laced excuse for a latte. Salt tasted overpowering, macha was great, but the sweetening wasn't there upon creation and the foam and latte mixture was non existent. No spices. Their daily drip is good. Service is ok, fast prompt. They could better label their natural sweetners

Aside from not being a Starbucks and being in the busiest shopping center in La Jolla it's just fine and dandy, but the lot parking sucks and their location and visibility do it no favors.<//text>

<Date>1398198606180< /Date><rate>4</rate>< Text>
Drinks: Caffe Latte
I consider myself a coffee drinker having atleast 1 morning  and 1 afternoon coffee daily. My visits to San Francisco would almost always have some Peet's in there. These have started popping up south allowing Angelinos and San Diegans to have the opportunity to try the Bucks alternative. This specific location in La Jolla is the closest to UCSD, so you can expect students everywhere with their textbooks. Most commented about the noise level, but what can you expect in such a populous coffee shop with nearly every seat filled. The lines on this Sunday morning were consistently 5 people long with most leaving immediately due to lack of seating. If there's one thing I like at Peet's better than Bucks, it's the Caffe Lattes. The frothiness in Peet's always seem to be tastier. I wouldn't go for anything sweeter on the menu for fear of completely converting to Peet's. The rewards program at Bucks, is truly what keeps me there.< /Text>

<name>Ashwin Mudigonda<//name>< Text>
Definitely better than Starbucks for one simple reason - free WiFi! Whereas Peet's website does not advertise that this particular store offers free WiFi, but it does, much to my surprise (and relief to my poor biking legs). However, the continuous background classical music and not so chill A/C knocks a star off from this place. The coffee is great...better than SB's! There is a motley crowd and a nice feel to the place. Having moved from the East coast, I miss the Caribou chain (free Wifi AND free refills for regular cofffee, as opposed to 90c per refill here) that is glaringly absent here. The tables feel a little small to use a laptop on and there are not convenient and enough power sockets to plug in.</Text>
